                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Fuk-thong pad khai Thai recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pumpkin #pork #eggs #fukthongpadkhai #fry #rice #oystersauce #fishsauce #egg #garlic #freerangeeggs \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Thai stir fried Pumpkin with egg is a delicious and simple Thai dish. It usually served with warm rice\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 975\n|PortionCalories = 243\n|DatePublished=24th October 2014\n|Author=Panrapee Satienpisarn\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  45 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Stir fired pumpkin with egg recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Good with courgettes too</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I made this with courgettes instead of pumpkin and it was rcoking!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Fuk-thong pad khai]] (Fuk-Thong means pumpkin in Thai) or Thai [[Stir-fried|stir fried]] [[Pumpkin]] with [[Egg|egg]] is a delicious and simple Thai dish. It usually served with warm [[Rice|rice]]. Pumpkin is the main [[Ingredient|ingredient]] and when purchasing the pumpkin it must be firm and heavy for its size. The best choice of [[pumpkin]] is Japanese pumpkin (kabocha). It is excellent for using in [[Soups|soups]], [[Stews|stews]] and [[Fry|fry]]. The flavour is sweet and tender. Pumpkin also has [[Vitamin A|vitamin a]], as well as, [[Vitamin C|vitamin c]], [[Phosphorus|phosphorus]], &#946;-carotene, [[Calcium|calcium]] and [[Flour|flour]]. It may reduce the chance of cancer, [[Heart|heart]] disease and anti-ageing.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 150 g [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork|pork]] (or [[Chicken|chicken]])\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]]\n| &#188; teaspoons [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| pinch of [[Pepper|pepper]]\n| 400 g Japanese [[pumpkin]] (kabocha)\n| 2 [[free range eggs]]\n| 1 - 2 [[Cloves garlic, minced|cloves garlic, minced]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 1 - 2 tablespoons [[Chopped spring onions|chopped spring onions]]\n| 100 ml water\n| 1 tablespoon [[Oyster sauce|oyster sauce]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| To prepare the [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]], remove [[Seeds|seeds]] and cut off the outside skin of the pumpkin. Then slice the pumpkin into 1-inch cubes and wash well with water.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a pan and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] until it becomes lightly [[Browned|browned]] and fragrant.\n| Add the [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork|pork]] to the pan wait until the pork nearly cooked.\n| Cut the [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] and place in a saucepan and cover with water. Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and cook until tender. When it is soft drain and then add to the [[Pork|pork]].\n| Crack the [[Eggs|eggs]] into the pan.\n| Once the [[Eggs|eggs]] are cooked, stir with [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] and [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork|pork]].\n| Add the other ingredients: [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]], [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Oyster sauce|oyster sauce]] and stir.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServed with warm [[Rice|rice]].\n==See also==\n\n* http://www.allaboutpumpkins.com/perfect.html, How to choose the perfect pumpkin, (4 September 2014)\n* http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2014/09/04/pumpkin-health-benefits_n_1936919.html, huffingtonpost, 8 Impressive Health Benefits of [[Pumpkin]], (7 September 2014)\n* http://shesimmers.com/2013/04/[[Stir-fried|stir fried]]-pumpkin-with-[[Eggs|eggs]]-.html, she simmers, Thai Stir-[[Fried]] [[Pumpkin]] with [[Egg]] (&#3612;&#3633;&#3604;&#3615;&#3633;&#3585;&#3607;&#3629;&#3591;&#3651;&#3626;&#3656;&#3652;&#3586;&#3656;), (7 September 2014)\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pumpkin #pork #eggs #fukthongpadkhai #fry #rice #oystersauce #fishsauce #egg #garlic #freerangeeggs </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It is available from all supermarkets and turns this simple dish into a very special meal.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g skinless, boneless [[Chicken|chicken]] breasts\n| 1 tablespoon [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n| 1 [[Egg white|egg white]], lightly beaten\n| 3 tablespoons [[Groundnut oil|groundnut oil]]\n| 4 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 2.5cm (1\") of fresh ginger, peeled and [[julienned]] \n| 4 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Sliced on the diagonal|sliced on the diagonal]]\n|* That's 4 if they are nice fat [[spring onions]], 8 or more if they are miserable examples from the supermarket!\n| 175 g (6 oz) [[Button mushrooms|button mushrooms]], sliced\n| 4 tablespoons [[Walnut|walnut]] pieces\n| 4 tablespoons [[hoisin sauce]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Whisk the [[Egg|egg]]-white, [[Cornflour|cornflour]] and [[Sherry|sherry]] in a bowl\n| Chop the [[Chicken|chicken]] into thin, bite-sized pieces and add to the bowl, mix well and leave to [[Marinade|marinade]] for 30 minutes or more.\n| Heat half of the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] until almost smoking and add the chicken, jiggle the wok a little to prevent the chicken sticking, but turn as little as possible. Stir-fry for 4 or 5 minutes or until the [[chicken]] is almost cooked. \n|Add the remaining [[oil]], throw in the [[ginger]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and half of the [[Spring onions|spring onions]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] until the [[Garlic|garlic]] starts to colour a little.\n|Add the [[mushrooms]] and [[walnuts]] and [[stir fry]] until the [[mushrooms]] wilt a little.\n|Pour the [[hoisin sauce]] over the [[chicken]] and heat until the [[hoisin sauce]] starts to bubble.\n| Serve immediately and sprinkle with the remaining [[spring onions]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nNice with [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]] or [[noodles]].\n===Variations===\n* Add a selection of your favourite vegetables at stage 5.\n* Add a few chopped [[Indian green chillies]] at stage 5 for a bit more bite.\n*Use [[shiitake mushrooms]] if you can get them.\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #hoisinsauce #springonions #hoisinchickenwithmushroomsandwalnuts #garlic #mushrooms #cornflour #noodles #marinade #walnut #drysherry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I have all of the whole ingredients in massive quantities, so thought it might be fun to make my own blend.\n\nThis recipe is only practical if you have the whole [[Spices|spices]] in large quantities, probably by buying from your local [[Chinese wholesalers]].  It would be expensive to make this from [[Spices|spices]] sold in those ridiculous little glass containers!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 4 teaspoons [[Szechuan peppercorns]] ( 8 grams )\n| 6 to 10 )\n| 2 teaspoons [[Fennel seeds|fennel seeds]] ( 8 grams )\n| 2 teaspoons [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]] ( 6 grams )\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Heat all of the ingredients in a small pan or [[Wok|wok]] for about 4 minutes or until the gorgeous aromas are released.\n| Allow to cool.\n| Blitz all of the ingredients to a powder in a [[coffee grinder]].\n| ''with this quantity of whole spices, it might be an idea to give the grinder a few minutes rest halfway through to save the motor''\n| Store in an airtight container.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nThe [[Coriander|coriander]] would not normally be found in [[5 spice powder]], I added it after reading comments from a reader and found that it added an interesting note so decided to include it in this mix.\n===Variations===\nTo aid other cooks in arriving at the perfect mix, I have included suggested mixes from other people which you may also like to try:\n=====5 spice powder, alternative mix #1=====\n:1 teaspoon ground [[Szechuan peppercorns]]\n:1 teaspoon ground [[star anise]]\n:1.25 teaspoon ground [[fennel seeds]]\n:0.5 teaspoon ground [[clove buds]]\n:0.5 teaspoon ground [[cinnamon]]\n:0.5 teaspoon [[table salt]]\n:0.25 teaspoon ground [[white pepper]]\n\n=====5 spice powder, alternative mix #2=====\n:2 teaspoons of [[Szechuan peppercorns]]\n:0.5 teaspoons of ground [[clove buds]]\n:1 tablespoon of ground [[cinnamon]]\n:8 whole [[star anise]], ground to a powder\n:1 tablespoon of ground [[fennel seeds]]\n\n=====5 spice powder, alternative mix #3=====\n:2 tablespoons ground [[star anise]]\n:2 tablespoons ground [[fennel seeds]]\n:2 teaspoons crushed [[cassia bark]] ([[cinnamon]] will a be fine substitute)\n:2 teaspoons crushed [[Szechuan peppercorns]]\n:0.25 teaspoon ground [[clove buds]]\n\n=====5 spice powder, alternative mix #4=====\n:4 teaspoon [[Szechuan peppercorns]]\n:16 whole [[star anise]]\n:12 [[clove buds]]\n:10 [[cinnamon sticks]]\n:2 tablespoons [[fennel seeds]]\n===Servings===\nServings: 20 - Makes 38 grams of homemade Chinese 5 spice powder\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese teaspoon [[salt]]\n| 2 free-range [[eggs]]\n}}\n'''for thickening'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 3 tablespoons [[white wine vinegar]]\n| 1.5 tablespoons [[dark soy sauce]]\n| &#189; teaspoon freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[cornflour]] blended to a paste with 3 tablespoons of water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Soak the mushrooms in boiled water for 20 minutes, squeeze excess water, remove stalks and slice thinly\n| Shred the cooked meat and [[bamboo shoots]]\n| Beat the [[eggs]]\n| Mix together the thickening ingredients\n| Heat the stock in a large pan\n| Add everything but the [[eggs]] and thickening, bring to the boil, cover simmer for 5 minutes\n| Pour in the thickening and stir until the consistency changes\n| Stir the soup so it rotates and gradually pour the [[eggs]] into the soup in a thin stream\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe immediately\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#hotandsoursoup #eggs #bambooshoots #whitewinevinegar #chicken #cornflour #ham #boiledorsimmered #darksoysauce #chinesemushrooms #blackpepper </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=How to make crispy aromatic duck at home a Chinese recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cucumber #springonions #duck #howtomakecrispyaromaticduckathome #foodprocessor #roastingtray #microwave #cheat #chinesepancakes #miseenplace #unusualrecipes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Please note: This recipe shows how to cook a ready prepared Peking-style duck and serve with the standard accompaniments\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n===How to make crispy aromatic duck at home===\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3520\n|PortionCalories = 880\n|DatePublished=4th February 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4 as a main\n |Difficulty = 1\n |ImageComment = Commercially prepared aromatic duck - \u00a35.20 <br> (Oriental Delight Wholesalers, Norwich 2019)\n |TotalTime = 1 hour\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 45 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Aromatic duck.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Just the best</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is so much better than the take-away version.  You can eat a whole duck for next to nothing this way. :D</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Chopped cucumber - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|[[Cucumber]], chopped|300px|thumb|right|Chopped [[cucumber]]]]\n[[Image:Chopped spring onions - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Spring onions, chopped|300px|thumb|right|[[Chopped spring onions]]]]\n[[Image:Chinese pancakes.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Frozen Chinese pancakes]]\n[[Image:Ready to go! - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Ready to go!]]\n''Please note:  This recipe shows how to cook a '''ready prepared Peking-style duck''' and serve with the standard accompaniments.   [[Peking duck|See here]] if you want to create this recipe from scratch using a fresh [[duck]].'' \n===A step by step guide, in pictures===\n<gallery widths=270px heights=270px perrow=5>\nImage:Spring onions - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|2 massive [[spring onions]]\nImage:Chopping spring onions - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|[[Cheat]], chop the [[spring onions]] in a [[food processor]]\nImage:Chopped spring onions - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Spring onions, chopped\nImage:Pretty-up the cucumber - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Pretty-up the [[cucumber]]\nImage:De-seed the cucumber- making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|De-seed the [[cucumber]], if you wish\nImage:Chopping the cucumber - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|[[Cheat]], chop the [[cucumber]] in a [[food processor]]\nImage:Chopped cucumber - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|[[Cucumber]], chopped\nImage:Crispy duck - cook from frozen - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Aromatic duck, cook from frozen\nImage:Duck ready for the oven - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Aromatic duck, ready for the over (200\u00b0 C for 45 minutes)\nImage:Crispy duck cooked - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Aromatic duck. Cooked\nImage:Shred the duck - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Shred the duck with two forks\nImage:Crispy duck pancakes- making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|[[Crispy duck pancakes]]\nImage:Warm the pancakes in the microwave- making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Warm them for a few seconds in the [[microwave]]\nImage:Sauce selection - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|The sauce selection\nImage:Ready to go! - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Ready to go\nImage:Spread the sauce - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Spread the sauce\nImage:Sprinkle the spring onions - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Sprinkle the [[spring onions]] on the pancake\nImage:Add the cucumber - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Add the sliced [[cucumber]]\nImage:Add the shredded crispy duck - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Top with shredded aromatic crispy duck\nImage:Ready to eat! - making crispy duck pancakes sequence.jpg|Rolled up and ready to eat\n</gallery>\n\nMaking this delicious Chinese take-away favourite at home is so simple and so reasonably priced that you'll never buy it from the take-away again.\n\nUnless you want to spend money for the sake of it, don't buy the ingredients from your local 'big-name' supermarket.  You'll probably pay double and certainly won't have the selection of ingredients that you'll have if you follow my next suggestion.\n===Buy the ingredients from the same place as your Chinese take-away does===\n''This advice is specific to the United Kingdom, though I'm sure similar outlets exist throughout the world''.\n\nPay a visit to your local [[Chinese food wholesaler]].  There are chains of them throughout the UK and you don't need to be a member of any trade association to buy from them.  You may find them a little intimidating at first, but the staff are friendly and if you are into your food in a big way, you will find it a fascinating experience.  Most of them have a very good online presence so you can 'look before you buy'.  I guarantee that you will go back again and again.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 800g frozen pre cooked aromatic crispy duck [\u00a39.50]\n| 1 multi-pack 'pancakes for crispy duck' [ 102 pancakes, 17 packs (pre-packed in packs of 6) ]\n| 1 [[cucumber]]\n| 1 bunch [[spring onions]]\n| 50g 'Sauce for Peking Duck'\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Defrost a few packets of [[Chinese pancakes]]\n* Peel the [[cucumber]], quarter lengthwise and run a sharp knife along each quadrant to remove most of the seeds.\n* Top and tail the [[spring onions]]\n* Using a [[food processor]] with a metal blade, slice the [[cucumber]] and [[spring onions]].  It doesn't look as neat as [[julienning]] them, but it takes a quarter of the time and tastes just as good.\n* Chill the [[spring onions]] and [[cucumber]] in the [[refrigerator]] while the [[duck]] defrosts\n* Preheat the oven to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[duck]] (skin-side down) on a rack over a [[roasting tray]] or a [[perforated roasting tray]] over a [[roasting tray]] - this will allow for the fat to drain off whilst the [[duck]] cooks.\n| Roast the [[duck]] for 45 minutes, turning once, carefully draining the roasting tray if it fills with [[fat]], otherwise you'll have a very smoky kitchen\n| You can [[steam]] the pancakes in a [[Chinese steamer]] over a [[wok]] or pan of boiling water for a few minutes - they only need to be warmed, not cooked.  I find they often stick together warming them this way so I prefer to separate the pancakes, spread them out on a large plate and [[microwave]] them for a minute or two to warm them.\n| Remove the [[duck]] from the oven, chop the skin into bite-sized pieces and then with two forks pulling against each other, shred the duck meat.\n}}\n===To serve===\nSpread a little of your favourite sauce on a pancake, cover with cucumber, spring onions & duck, roll the pancake up and eat with your fingers - delicious!\n===Variations===\nTry other sauces: [[Hoisin sauce]], [[Plum sauce]], [[chilli sauce]] and even [[mayonaise]] works very well!\n\nSliced white [[onions]] are a nice addition to [[spring onions]].\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Duck]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes|Duck]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes|Duck]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Duck]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Duck]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Duck]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Duck]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cucumber #springonions #duck #howtomakecrispyaromaticduckathome #foodprocessor #roastingtray #microwave #cheat #chinesepancakes #miseenplace #unusualrecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Khanom Tom",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Thai coconut balls (Khanom Tom), Thai dessert recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#khanomtom #coconut #grated #pandanus #flour #dough #glutinousrice #brownsugar #juice #dessert #coconutcream \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Khanom Tom (Thai : \u0e02\u0e19\u0e21\u0e15\u0e49\u0e21) or coconut balls are a very old Thai dessert from the Sukhothai period and are used for auspicious ceremonies\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1739\n|PortionCalories = 217\n|DatePublished=30th October 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 8\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  30 minutes\n|PrepTime =  20 minutes\n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:glutinous rice balls for dessert.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n}}\n[[Khanom Tom]] ([[Thai]] : \u0e02\u0e19\u0e21\u0e15\u0e49\u0e21) or [[Coconut|coconut]] balls are a very old Thai [[Dessert|dessert]] from the Sukhothai period and are traditionally used for auspicious ceremonies. Khanom tom consist of [[Glutinous rice|glutinous rice]] [[Flour|flour]] , [[Grated|grated]] coconut , [[Pandanus|pandanus]] [[Juice|juice]] , [[Salt|salt]] , and [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]. Khanom Tom is sweet-smelling, sweet and the texture is smooth ,soft and sticky.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 cup [[Glutinous rice|glutinous rice]] [[Flour|flour]] \n| 2 tablespoons [[Coconut cream|coconut cream]] \n| 100 grams white [[Grated|grated]] [[Coconut|coconut]] (for the filling) \n| 1 cup white [[Grated|grated]] [[Coconut|coconut]] (for the coating) \n| \u00bd cup [[Sugar|sugar]] \n| \u00bd teaspoon [[Salt|salt]] \n| \u00bc cup thick [[Pandanus|pandanus]] [[Juice|juice]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Putting the [[Grated|grated]] [[Coconut|coconut]] in the pot and [[Steam|steam]] until hot.\n| Mix in the [[Salt|salt]] and set aside.\n| Make a filling by mixing [[Grated|grated]] [[Coconut|coconut]] with [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]] on a medium heat and stir until the [[Sugar|sugar]] has dissolved\n| Remove from the heat, allow to cool a little and make by [[Hand|hand]] into small balls.\n| Make the [[Dough|dough]] by [[Kneading|kneading]] [[Glutinous rice|glutinous rice]] [[Flour|flour]] , [[Coconut cream|coconut cream]] , [[Pandanus|pandanus]] juice and a little water.\n| Make the [[Dough|dough]] into a ball and press to flatten. Fill with the filling and wrap dough to cover it.\n| [[Boil]] the [[Dough|dough]] to ball in. You can [[Scoop|scoop]] out them when they float. Lastly, roll with the [[Steamed|steamed]] [[Grated|grated]] [[Coconut|coconut]].\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* [[Khanom Tom]] - [[Pandanus]] [[Rice]] Balls,(n.d.), Retrieved October 15,2014 [https://www.achefshelp.com/recipe/331/pandanus-rice-ballskhanom-tom-bai-toei-[[Dessert|dessert]]-[[Thailand|thailand]]-worldwide-recipes]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">No accounting for taste</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">2</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not for me I'm afraid.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#khanomtom #coconut #grated #pandanus #flour #dough #glutinousrice #brownsugar #juice #dessert #coconutcream </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Kuay Teow Kua Gai",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Kuay Teow Kua Gai (Fried rice noodles with chicken) recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#kuayteowkuagai #chicken #oystersauce #lettuce #squid #vinegar #tomato #ricenoodles #cabbage #lightsoysauce #wok \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Fried rice noodles with chicken or Kuay Teow Kua Gai (Thai : \u0e01\u0e4b\u0e27\u0e22\u0e40\u0e15\u0e35\u0e4b\u0e22\u0e27\u0e04\u0e31\u0e48\u0e27\u0e44\u0e01\u0e48) is a Chinese-influenced dish with Noodles\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1928\n|PortionCalories = 482\n|DatePublished=23rd October 2014\n|Author=Panrapee Satienpisarn\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  10 minutes\n|PrepTime =   5 minutes\n|CookTime =  5 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Kuay Teow Kua Gai recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n}}\nStir-fried [[rice noodles]] with [[chicken]], Fried rice noodles with [[chicken]] or Kuay Teow Kua Gai (Thai : \u0e01\u0e4b\u0e27\u0e22\u0e40\u0e15\u0e35\u0e4b\u0e22\u0e27\u0e04\u0e31\u0e48\u0e27\u0e44\u0e01\u0e48) is a Chinese-influenced dish with Noodles or Kuay Teow that is popular in Thailand. Kuay teow was later modified by Thais to dried noodles with chicken. Then, they call this style \"Kuay Teow Kua Gai\". Kuay Teow Kua Gai normally is served as soaked dried rice noodles stirred with a simple combination of ingredients, such as [[chicken]], [[squid]] and [[lettuce]]. You can add other additional ingredients as sliced [[tomatoes]], [[egg]], deep-fried doughstick, [[garlic]]  and [[spring onion]]. It is seasoned with [[oyster sauce]], [[light soy sauce]] and fish sauce. It also may be seasoned with sauce prik (''nam prik - [[chilli sauce]]''), [[chili flakes]], [[vinegar]], [[sugar]] and tangy [[tomato sauce]].\n\nTo make this dish special is arrange the Kuay Teow Kua Gai on the top of [[lettuce]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n|\u00bd kilo of [[rice noodle]] (Depends on you)\n|\u00bd cup of sliced chicken\n|\u00bd cup of [[squid]] \n|3 chicken [[eggs]] \n|Sliced [[Tomato]]\n|1 teaspoon of dry [[cabbage]] leaves\n|1 tablespoon of chopped [[spring onions]]\n|2-3 tablespoons of frying [[oil]]\n|1 tablespoon of [[oyster sauce]]\n|1 tablespoon of [[fish sauce]]\n|2 tablespoons of [[oyster sauce]]\n|1 tablespoon of [[soy sauce]]\n|1 tablespoon of [[white sugar]]\n|[[Chinese cabbage]] (depends on you)\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the oil to your [[wok]]\n| Add the onions and vegetables and stir fry for 3 minutes\n| Add the meat or fish and stir fry for a few more minutes\n| Pour in the liquid ingredients and mix well\n| ''You can add the egg and scramble it in the pan, then mix it up, or just add it and stir-fry it as it cooks''\n}}\n\n\n=== See also ===\n\n*http://www.ucancookthai.com/language-thai/th-recipes/th-noodle/content-th-stir fried-chicken-noodle.htm  ,\u0e01\u0e4b\u0e27\u0e22\u0e40\u0e15\u0e35\u0e4b\u0e22\u0e27\u0e04\u0e31\u0e48\u0e27\u0e44\u0e01\u0e48 (October 06, 2009) <br>\n*http://naeskitchen.blogspot.com/2010/03/fried-rice-noodles-with-chicken-thai.html ,\u0e01\u0e4b\u0e27\u0e22\u0e40\u0e15\u0e35\u0e4b\u0e22\u0e27\u0e04\u0e31\u0e48\u0e27\u0e44\u0e01\u0e48 - Fried rice noodles with chicken Thai style - Massa de arroz frita com galinha (Nae's Kitchen, MARCH 29, 2010)\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Looks and tastes authentic</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Putting this on a bed of lettuce sounded odd, but it works really well, strangely.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#kuayteowkuagai #chicken #oystersauce #lettuce #squid #vinegar #tomato #ricenoodles #cabbage #lightsoysauce #wok </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Kuay teow lot",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Kuay teow lot Thai recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#kuayteowlot #garlic #noodle #lettuce #shrimp #pork #carrot #tofu #oystersauce #darksoysauce #coriander \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Kuay Teow Lot is a one dish Thai food. Kuay Teow Lot in the mean in Thai is a noodle tube shape, but it doesn't look like a tube!\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 5550\n|PortionCalories = 370\n|DatePublished=24th October 2014\n|Author=Panrapee Satienpisarn\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 15\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 24 minutes \n|PrepTime = 12 minutes\n|CookTime = 12 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Kuay Teow Lot.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Just like the real thing</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I could be in Chiang Mai \ud83c\udf5c</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Kuay Teow Lot]] is a one dish Thai food. Kuay Teow Lot in the mean in Thai is a [[Noodle|noodle]] tube shape, but actuality it doesn't look like a tube. Why then did they choose this name? May be in the past they like to use a sheet of [[Noodles|noodles]] and add the filling then roll it. The shape will be thin and long look like a tube, but nowadays people like to wrap it in a square size fit mouth same as Miang Kham, Kuay Teow Lui Suan or Fresh spring roll.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| Sheet of [[Noodle|noodle]] \u00bd kg \n| [[Minced]] [[Pork|pork]] 700 g \n| [[Shrimp]] 500 g \n| [[Mushroom]] 200 g\n| [[Tofu]] 2 sheets\n| [[Pickle]] [[Turnip|turnip]] \u00bc cup\n| Water 3 cup\n| [[Garlic]] 2 tablespoon\n| [[Coriander]] root 1 tablespoon\n| [[Oil]] 2 tablespoon\n| [[Light soy sauce]] \u00bc cup\n| [[Dark soy sauce]] 1 tablespoon\n| [[Oyster sauce]] 2 tablespoon\n| [[Sugar]] \u00bd cup\n| [[Carrot]] 150 g\n| [[Bean sprouts]] 1 kg\n| [[Lettuce]] 200 g\n}}\n'''sauce'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Chilli]] 1 g\n| [[Garlic]] 1 tablespoon\n| [[Vinegar]] 1/3 cup\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Heat [[Oil|oil]] in the pan and [[Fry|fry]] [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Coriander|coriander]] [[Roots|roots]], [[Tofu|tofu]], [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork|pork]], [[Shrimp|shrimp]], [[Mushroom|mushroom]] and [[Lettuce|lettuce]] fry together \n| [[Boiling]] three cups of water, add a [[Carrot|carrot]] cut into a small square pieces and then [[Boil|boil]] until soft. Put an ingredient from the first stage into the pot and mix together and then season with a [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]], [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]], [[Oyster sauce|oyster sauce]] and [[Sugar|sugar]] when it boils take off the [[Stove|stove]]. \n| Put the mixture onto a [[Noodle|noodle]] sheets then roll it to be tight. Next [[Steam|steam]] for about 3 minutes when finish slice as you like decorating your plate with [[Lettuce|lettuce]].\n| Finally eat with [[Sauce|sauce]].\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* \u0e23\u0e34\u0e0d \u0e40\u0e08\u0e23\u0e34\u0e0d\u0e28\u0e34\u0e23\u0e34, \u0e2d\u0e17\u0e34\u0e15\u0e14\u0e32 \u0e1a\u0e38\u0e0d\u0e1b\u0e23\u0e30\u0e40\u0e14\u0e34\u0e21 (September 1,2008) \u201c[[Kuay Teow Lot]]\u201d http://www.doctor.or.th/article/detail/5756\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#kuayteowlot #garlic #noodle #lettuce #shrimp #pork #carrot #tofu #oystersauce #darksoysauce #coriander </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Kung Po chicken",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Kung Po chicken, Chinese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#kungpochicken #chicken #carrots #cornflour #toasted #eggfriedrice #onions #garlic #sesameoil #cashewnuts #wok \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Kung Po chicken (also spelled Kung Pao chicken) is a classic dish in Szechuan cuisine, originating in the Sichuan Province of central western China\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1185\n|PortionCalories = 296\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |ImageComment = Kung po chicken & [[egg fried rice]]\n |TotalTime = 1 hour\n |PrepTime = 40 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Kung po chicken recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">My favourite Chinese meal</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Nicer than the gloopy versions sold at some take-aways.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]])</span></span>\n }}\nKung Po chicken (also spelled Kung Pao chicken) is a classic dish in Szechuan cuisine, originating in the Sichuan Province of central western China. The dish is named after Ding Baozhen (1820\u20131886), a late Qing Dynasty official. Born in Guizhou, Ding served as head of Shandong province and later as governor of Sichuan province. His title was G&#333;ng B&#462;o (&#23470;&#20445;), or palatial guardian. The name \"Kung Pao\" chicken is derived from this title.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450g (1 lb) [[chicken]], cubed\n| 1 egg white\n| 1 teaspoon [[salt]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[cornflour]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[groundnut oil]]\n| 8 hot [[dried chili peppers]] (or to taste)\n| Handful of [[toasted]] [[cashew nuts]], unsalted if possible\n| 1 small [[onion]], sliced\n| 2 small [[carrots]], [[julienned]] and then chopped\n| 1 teaspoon minced [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[light soy sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[rice wine]] or [[dry sherry]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[sugar]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[white wine vinegar]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[sesame oil]]\n| 3 tablespoons of water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a bowl, mix the egg white, salt and half the [[cornflour]], then coat the cubed chicken pieces with this mixture and leave to [[marinate]] for 30 minutes\n| Heat the oil in a wok and fry the [[onions]] and [[carrots]] for 4 minutes and reserve\n| Fry the chicken until lightly browned then remove from pan\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and chillies and [[stir-fry]] for 2 minutes\n| Return the [[chicken]], [[onions]] and [[carrots]] to the [[wok]] and add the [[soy sauce]], [[wine]], [[sugar]], [[vinegar]] and [[sesame oil]] and stir-fry for 2 minutes\n| In a saucer, mix the remaining [[cornflour]] and water into a smooth paste\n| Add the paste to the [[wok]] and mix well\n| Simmer, stirring as required, until the sauce clears and the [[chicken]] is properly cooked\n| Add the [[toasted]] [[cashew nuts]] just before serving to ensure they stay crunchy\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Plain rice|plain rice]] or [[egg fried rice]]\n===Chef's notes===\nCarrots and onions may not be authentic, but I like the colour and crunch of the carrots and the taste of the onions.\n\nIf you really don't like crunchy carrots, you may want to [[parboil]] them for a few minutes before you start cooking the dish.\n\n==See also==\n\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]][[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#kungpochicken #chicken #carrots #cornflour #toasted #eggfriedrice #onions #garlic #sesameoil #cashewnuts #wok </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

title": "Nam phrik kaeng som",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Nam phrik kaeng som recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chilies #shallots #shrimppaste #namphrikkaengsom #fishsauce #pestleandmortar #unusualrecipes #sauce #chili #mortarandpestle #garlic \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Nam Prik Kaeng Som (Thai Sour curry paste) is the base sauce for many Thai curries\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 132\n|PortionCalories = 16\n|DatePublished=27th October 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Nam phrik kapi (foreground)\n|Servings = Servings: 8 - Makes one batch\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  13 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  3 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Nam_phrik_kapi.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Must have Thai fish sauce</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">It's the only way to make this authentic.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nNam Prik Kaeng Som (Thai Sour [[Curry paste|curry paste]])\n\nThis is the base [[Sauce|sauce]] for many Thai [[Curries|curries]].\n\nNam phrik (Thai: \u0e19\u0e49\u0e33\u0e1e\u0e23\u0e34\u0e01, pronounced [n\u00e1m p\u02b0r\u00edk], lit. \"fluid chili\") is a generic term that may refer to any of the types of more or less viscous, spicy, [[chili]]-based, hot sauces typical of [[Thai cuisine]]. Usual ingredients for nam phrik are fresh or dry [[chilies]], [[garlic]], [[shallots]], [[lime juice]] and often some kind of fish or [[shrimp paste]]. In the traditional way of preparing the sauce, the ingredients are pounded together using a [[mortar and pestle]], with either [[salt]] or [[fish sauce]] added to taste.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 10 [[Dried]] [[Chilies|chilies]]\n| 5 [[Shallots]], chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Shrimp paste]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Salt]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Coarsely chop the [[Chilies|chilies]] and soak in water for 10 minutes.  Drain.\n| Combine all of the ingredients into a paste, using a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThis sauce goes well with fish and vegetables and is the base for many Thai curries such as [[Thai Moringa curry with shrimp]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n===Reference===\n* [http://www.recipesource.com/ethnic/asia/thai/02/rec0250.html www.recipesource.com/ethnic/asia/thai/02/rec0250.html]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chilies #shallots #shrimppaste #namphrikkaengsom #fishsauce #pestleandmortar #unusualrecipes #sauce #chili #mortarandpestle #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Oriental sous vide silverside beef",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Oriental sous vide silverside beef recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#beef #szechuanpeppercorns #orientalsousvidesilversidebeef #vacuumsealer #marinade #fineyellowcornmeal #lightsoysauce #shoyo #pestleandmortar #shoyubeef #fat \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe is similar to Shoyu beef, which is distinctly Japanese. I thought I would try a similar recipe using sous vide cooking and using everyday\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2350\n|PortionCalories = 1175\n|DatePublished=16th February 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2 with leftovers!\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  12 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  12 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Oriental sous vide silverside beef recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Slice it thin!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This was much nicer when we cut it thin with a proper meat slicer.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Sous vide silverside.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Silverside joint sealed ready for the sous vide oven]]\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nThis recipe is similar to [[Shoyu beef]], which is distinctly Japanese.  I thought I would try a similar recipe using sous vide cooking and using everyday ingredients as some of the Japanese ingredients can be difficult to find.  I also wanted to experiment with this sous vide recipe using relatively  economic silverside of [[Beef|beef]] rather than beef fillet.\n\nI've used Chardonnay instead of [[Mirin]], not a great substitute but I always have some Chardonnay in the freezer in paper cups.  Dead easy to scoop a spoonful out when needed for cooking, and it saves having to drink the dreadful stuff! [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]] is pretty close to [[shoyo]].  I use [[Frozen ginger paste]] which is almost as good as the real thing.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 700g [1lb 8 oz] [[Beef|beef]] silverside joint, trimmed of excess [[Fat|fat]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[White wine|white wine]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger|ginger]] (thumb sized piece of ginger, peeled and grated)\n| 1/4 of a teaspoon [[Szechuan peppercorns|szechuan peppercorns]] crushed in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n| 1 tablespoon of [[fine yellow cornmeal]] to thicken the gravy, optional.\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Stamp the joint all over with a [[meat tenderiser]] tool. This helps to tenderize the joint and also allow the [[Marinade|marinade]] to permeate the meat.\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| When selecting the size of pouch to contain the [[Beef|beef]], make one that is quite a bit larger than the joint.  This seems to make it easier to seal without drawing all the [[Marinade|marinade]] into the [[Vacuum sealer|vacuum sealer]].\n| Being careful not to wet the inner edges of the bag where it will be sealed, add all of the ingredients, apart from the cornmeal to the vacuum bag.\n| Set the [[Vacuum sealer|vacuum sealer]] so the bag can hang vertically over the edge of the work surface.\n| Press the [[Vacuum seal|vacuum seal]] button on your sealer and then cancel just as any liquid begins to be drawn into the sealing chamber.  Then press heat seal to seal the bag.  The pessimist in me always seals the bag a couple of times at each end, just in case!\n| Sous vide cook at 68\u00b0C (''154.4\u00b0F'') for 12 hours for medium - well done.  See [[Sous vide cooking times]] for other levels of doneness.\n| If you want to thicken the gravy, immediately the 12 hours cooking is complete, add the juices to a hot pan together with a tablespoon of [[fine yellow cornmeal]], bring to a simmer, stirring all the while.\n| Carve and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and a [[Vegetable|vegetable]] of your choice.\n===Chef's notes===\nThis was fantastic, the meat was so tender and juicy that it didn't really need any gravy.  I've now reduced the quantity of the [[szechuan peppercorns]] as they were a little overpowering.  Any strong flavours multiply when cooking in a vac packed bag.\n\nI've not found any benefit to resting meat when cooking [[sous vide]] and in this instance I did not sear the outside of the meat as it looked great with all the peppercorns around the edge.\n{{SousVideSeeAlso}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Sous vide recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide cooking]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beef #szechuanpeppercorns #orientalsousvidesilversidebeef #vacuumsealer #marinade #fineyellowcornmeal #lightsoysauce #shoyo #pestleandmortar #shoyubeef #fat </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Will be made again!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe is usually cooked by [[Simmering|simmering]] for an hour or so, but recently I've had such a success with [[Pressure cooking|pressure cooking]] [[Beef|beef]] [[Stews|stews]] I thought it worth a try with this as it has such strong flavours, which are unlikely to be reduced by the relative long cooking time.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 400 g lean [[Stewing|stewing]] [[Beef|beef]] ([[Flank|flank]] is ideal)\n| 2 thumb-sized pieces of [[Ginger|ginger]], thinly sliced.\n| ..don't worry about peeling the [[Ginger|ginger]], most of it can be picked out before serving, or eaten anyway.\n| Good pinch of freshly [[Ground|ground]] [[Szechuan peppercorns]]\n| 4 large bulb [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Chopped on the diagonal|chopped on the diagonal]]\n| 360 ml water\n| 50 ml [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| 50 ml [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n| 50 ml [[Rice wine|rice wine]] or pale [[Cream Sherry|cream sherry]]\n| 1 tablespoon soft [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Place all of the ingredients in a bowl and mix well\n| Pop the bowl on a trivet in your [[Pressure cooker|pressure cooker]]\n| ..I have modified a small [[Saucepan|saucepan]] so it can be easily removed from the [[Pressure cooker|pressure cooker]], though a [[Pyrex bowl]] would be fine\n| Pressure cook on a high setting for one hour\n| Allow to depressurise naturally\n| Serve!\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Red cooked beef with ginger before any cooking.jpg|Prepared and ready for the pressure cooker\nImage:Out of the pressure cooker in my modified pressure cooker saucepan.jpg|Cooked, in my saucepan I modified to fit in a pressure cooker\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nI would normally serve this with [[Rice|rice]] and [[Vegetables|vegetables]] but we fancied [[Air fried roast potatoes|air-fried]] roasties this time.\n===Chef's notes===\nThis could be cooked by bringing to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmering|simmering]] for an hour or so, but it won't be as tender as the relative extended cooking time in a [[Pressure cooker|pressure cooker]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Beef The salt helps to remove a little of the moisture so firming the flesh\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1528\n|PortionCalories = 382\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 40 minutes plus 2 or more hours marinading\n|PrepTime = 10 minutes plus 2 or more hours marinading\n|CookTime = 30 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Rock salmon with garlic and coriander.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A faded memory</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I really don't remember making this, but the camera never lies. gas 4) after step 4\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Generously season the [[Rock salmon|rock salmon]] with [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| Drizzle the [[Citrus|citrus]] juice, [[Zest|zest]] and [[Nam pla|nam pla]] over the [[Fish|fish]]\n| Roll the [[Fish|fish]] in the marinade to ensure it's well coated\n| Refrigerate for an hour or two\n| In a pan, gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] in the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] until soft, about 4 minutes\n| Stir in the [[Chilli|chilli]] flakes, [[Ginger root|ginger root]] and any juice\n| [[Oil]] a small ovenproof dish and lay the [[Fish|fish]] in it together with the juices\n| Cover with the [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and then ladle the [[Onion|onion]] mixture over the top\n| [[Bake]] uncovered for 20 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot, with [[Lime|lime]] or [[Orange|orange]] [[Wedges|wedges]] and [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]].\n\n===Variations===\n\nUse [[basa]], [[ling]], [[Halibut|halibut]] or [[conger eel]] as an alternate fish for this dish\n\nHaving a fridge clean, I added a chopped [[sweet pepper]] and a few [[celery]] sticks at the same time as the [[onions]] and [[garlic]].\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#orange #fish #onion #rocksalmonwithgarlicandcoriander #garlic #lime #gingerroot #oliveoil #nampla #zest #chilli </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Because the [[beef]] is only cooked for a short time, it's worth using high quality beef such as fillet for this dish.\n[[Image:Seared beef and beanspouts with spicy lime dressing recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ingredients for seared [[beef]] and [[bean sprouts]] in a spicy lime dressing]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) [[beef]] fillet steak, cut into 2.5 cm (1\") steaks\n| 115 g (4 oz) [[bean sprouts]]\n| 4 or 5 [[button mushrooms]]\n| Big handful of [[basil leaves]]\n| Big handful of [[mint leaves]]\n| 1 [[lime]], quartered for garnish\n| [[Peanut oil]] for [[frying]]\n| '''For the [[marinade]]'''\n| 2 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, crushed\n| [[Zest]] of 2 [[limes]]\n| Juice of 2 [[limes]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[nuoc mam]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[jaggery]]\n| 1 [[lemongrass]] stalk, bruised and chopped\n| 2 small hot [[red chillies]], deseeded and sliced into rings\n| 3 spring onions, [[sliced on the diagonal]]\n}}\n===Method===\n'''The [[marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Whisk the [[lime juice]] and [[zest]], [[jaggery]] and [[nuoc mam]] until the [[jaggery]] dissolves\n| (if the [[jaggery]] is solid and hard, first crush it with the end of a rolling pin)\n| Mix in the crushed [[Garlic|garlic]], [[chillies]] and [[lemongrass]]\n}}\n\n'''The beef'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a hot pan with a little [[oil]], sear the fillets for 2 minutes per side, remove and allow to cool\n| Cut the [[meat]] into thin slices\n| Add to the [[marinade]] an refrigerate for at least 2 hours\n| Blanch the [[bean sprouts]] for 1 minutes in just [[boiled]] water. Allow to cool then arrange in a large serving bowl with the mint, basil and the chopped [[spring onions]].\n| After 2 hours, drain excess liquid from the [[meat]] and arrange in the bowl with the [[bean sprouts]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nGarnish with [[lime]] slices and serve with [[coconut rice]]\n===Chef's notes===\n\nI also added some raw sliced [[button mushrooms]] to the [[bean sprouts]] because I happened to have some left over.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Beef]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Beef]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters|Beef]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Indonesian recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beansprouts #jaggery #beef #marinade #limes #zest #lemongrass #lime #garlic #nuocmam #buttonmushrooms </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Sichuan chili oil",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sichuan chili oil, Chinese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#sichuanpeppercorns #sichuanchilioil #chinesecuisine #peanutoil #celsius #sesameoil #sieve #thermometer #degrees #refrigerator #chiliflakes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe together with all of the photographs, is taken directly from Robin's cookery blog\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2041\n|PortionCalories = 11\n|DatePublished=17th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = 350 ml bottle of chilli oil\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 1 hour incl. cooling\n |PrepTime = 50 minutes\n |CookTime = 10 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Hot Chili oil.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lip-tingling!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Superb way to get my Szechuan pepper-fix.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe together with all of the photographs, is taken directly from [[User:Robin|Robin's]] cookery blog: [http://kokrobin.wordpress.com/ Kok Robin]\nTo quote [[User:Robin|Robin]]:\n''\"The combination of [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Sichuan peppercorns|sichuan peppercorns]] is just divine. And so typical of [[Sichuan cuisine|sichuan cuisine]].\n\nI used to live in Beijing for 2.5 years. In this time I absolutely fell in love with [[Chinese cuisine]], but sichuan cuisine in particular. And the sichuan [[Peppercorn|peppercorn]] is largely responsible for that. I just love the tingly, numbing, citrusy, sharp taste.''\n\n''So I was delighted to discover this homemade [[Chili oil|chili oil]]. To me, it's simply Sichuan in a Bottle.\"''\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 6 tablespoons [[Sichuan peppercorns|sichuan peppercorns]] (pictured)\n| 8 tablespoons [[Chili flakes|chili flakes]] (ready bought or chop some [[Dried chillies|dried chillies]] yourself)\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]]\n| 360 ml [[Peanut oil|peanut oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put everything except the [[Oil|oil]] in a heat proof container.\n| Heat [[Oil|oil]] between 107 to 122.5 [[Degrees|degrees]] [[Celsius]] and pour over the other ingredients. Be careful because it will sizzle. (Or actually, when you have a [[Thermometer|thermometer]], like I do, you will notice it won't sizzle at all. If you don't, then yes, be careful)\n| Leave to cool down. After the flavours have blended for a day you can [[Sieve|sieve]] the [[Oil|oil]], if you wish. \n|Store in your [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]] for a couple of weeks.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Szechuan chilli oil - heated.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Heating the chillies and peppercorns\nImage:Szechuan chilli oil - cold.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Opaque when taken from the fridge\n</gallery>\n===Robin's notes===\nFunny thing is that with my version it always \u201csets\u201d.\n\nWhen I take it out of the fridge it will become nice and translucent again, but cold it looks like this.\n\nI\u2019m quite sure it doesn\u2019t make any difference to the taste, but if anybody knows why this happens, please tell me! (*edit* It\u2019s the type of oil) \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:FotoosVanRobin recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sichuanpeppercorns #sichuanchilioil #chinesecuisine #peanutoil #celsius #sesameoil #sieve #thermometer #degrees #refrigerator #chiliflakes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The duck meat was almost like liver!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 [[Duck|duck]] legs, skin on\n| 2 whole [[Star anise|star anise]]\n| Pinch of hickory smoke powder\n| 1 teaspoon soft [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| 10 [[Szechuan peppercorns|szechuan peppercorns]]\n| 10 [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]]\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Harissa seasoning|harissa seasoning]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Spices|spices]] apart from the [[Star anise|star anise]] to a fine powder in a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]]\n| Coat the [[Duck|duck]] legs with the [[Spice|spice]] powder\n| Pop the [[Duck|duck]] legs, sliced [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]] in to a [[Lock and Lock]] box, cover and shake well\n| [[Refrigerate]] the spicy legs for 10 hours or until you're ready to cook them\n| After 10 hours, drain any excess liquid and seal the duck legs in a [[Vacuum seal|vacuum seal]] bag\n| Cook in a [[Sous-vide bath|sous-vide bath]] for 10 hours at 82\u00b0C (179.6\u00b0F)\n| After cooking, discard the [[Star anise|star anise]], pat the legs [[Dry|dry]] and crisp the skin with a Map Gas [[Blow torch|blow torch]]\n| The Map Gas torches do not taint the food, which some blowtorches do\n| Serve!\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\n</gallery>\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main title": "Sous vide hoisin duck breasts",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sous vide hoisin sauce duck breast recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#duck #sear #sousvidehoisinduckbreasts #toastedsesameseeds #sesameoil #hoisinsauce #blackricevinegar #wok #stirfry #slowcooker #sousvidecooking \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The most tender duck breasts you will ever taste, cooked sous vide.  Temperatures and times with photographs\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n==Sous vide hoisin duck breasts==\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1143\n|PortionCalories = 571\n|DatePublished=4th February 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 2 hours 15 minutes\n|PrepTime = 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 2 hours 5 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Sous vide hoisin duck breasts recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Noodles and hoisin!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Yummily.  This was very special.  Try it!!!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nFlushed with the absolute success cooking [[Lamb chops|lamb chops]] in my homemade sous vide [[Slow cooker|slow cooker]] conversion kit, I think [[Duck|duck]] is next.\n\nThis time I wanted to add some flavours to the vacuum sealed pouches and as [[Hoisin|hoisin]] works so well with [[Duck|duck]], I thought I would try that.  I also added a teaspoon of Chinkiang black vice [[Vinegar|vinegar]] as I love its subtle flavour and in may [[Tenderise|tenderise]] the duck a little too.  It is likely that most of the vinegar is likely to be sucked out of the pouch during the vacuum process, so to this end I used enough plastic to make a pouch that would hang over the edge of the counter top whilst sealing, hopefully to lessen the effect.\n\nThis was a superb meal.  The duck breast was so tender you could have pushed your finger through it.  It had the flavour and mouthfeel of a rare duck breast, without all that blood.  Marvellous!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 310g [[Duck|duck]] breasts, skin on [2]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Hoisin sauce|hoisin sauce]]\n| 2 teaspoons Chinkiang [[Black rice vinegar|black rice vinegar]]\n}}\n''' to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 packet prepared [[Stir fry|stir fry]] mix.  Yes, I know it's [[Cheating|cheating]], but it is a weekday!\n| 160g [[Egg noodles|egg noodles]] (about 2 'nests')\n| 1 tablespoon [[Toasted sesame seeds|toasted sesame seeds]]\n| [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* If you are luck enough to have a [[Jaccard meat tenderiser]], stamp the breast all over on the skin side to puncture the skin and provide a path for the flavours to penetrate the [[Meat|meat]].\n* Make up 2 vacuum pouches that will be large enough to [[Hand|hand]] over the counter top while the breasts are being sealed.\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Browning the duck breasts.jpg|Browning the duck breasts on both sides\nImage:Hang the duck breast pouches over the worktop.jpg|Hang the pouches over the worktop to try to prevent sucking all of the marinade out of the pouch\nImage:Duck breasts Jaccard meat tenderizer.jpg|Stamp the duck breasts with the Jaccard meat tenderiser\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Place a teaspoon of [[Hoisin sauce|hoisin sauce]] and a teaspoon of Chinkiang [[Black rice vinegar|black rice vinegar]] in each pouch \n| Pop a [[Duck|duck]] breast in each pouch and wipe the inside of the pouch where it will be sealed with a [[Paper towel|paper towel]].\n| Hang the pouch over the edge of the countertop and [[Vacuum seal|vacuum seal]].\n| Set your sous vide bath to 56.5\u00b0C (''133.7\u00b0F'')\n| Suspend the pouches in the bath and heat for 2 hours\n| When the [[Duck|duck]] breasts have cooked, get a heavy based [[Frying pan|frying pan]] very hot with no [[Oil|oil]] and [[Sear|sear]] the duck breasts, skin side down for 2 minutes\n| If you have a mapp [[Blowtorch|blow torch]] you can [[Sear|sear]] the [[Meat|meat]] side of the breast while the skin is being crisped.  I wouldn't bother with a propane blowtorch unless you like the taste of propane fuel.\n| Meanwhile cook your [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] mix in a hot [[Wok|wok]] with a little [[Oil|oil]] and pop the [[Noodle|noodle]] nests in [[Boiling|boiling]] water for 4 minutes.\n| Drain and toss in [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]] and a teaspoon of [[Toasted sesame seeds|toasted sesame seeds]].\n| Slice the [[Duck|duck]] breasts diagonally into bite-size pieces and serve.\n}}\n{{SousVideSeeAlso}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide cooking]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#duck #sear #sousvidehoisinduckbreasts #toastedsesameseeds #sesameoil #hoisinsauce #blackricevinegar #wok #stirfry #slowcooker #sousvidecooking </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

This would last 2 people a couple of days if you keep the dressing and [[Spices|spices]] in a [[Air-tight container|airtight containers]] and only cut the [[Vegetable|vegetables]] up when ready to use them.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 4 [[Chicken breast|chicken breast]] fillets cut into thin slices\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to [[Fry|fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces\n}}\n'''[[Chicken|chicken]] [[Marinade|marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 4 [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sesame oil|sesame oil]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n}}\n'''[[Salad|salad]] items'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| &#189; cup of [[Cashew nuts|cashew nuts]], [[Dry-roasted|dry-roasted]] and crushed\n| 4 [[Shallots|shallots]], peeled and very thinly sliced\n| 10 whole baby [[sweetcorn]] cobs, thinly sliced\n| 1 stalk of [[Lemongrass|lemongrass]] very thinly sliced\n| 3 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], sliced\n| 1 teaspoon fresh [[Galangal|galangal]], peeled and chopped\n| 2 fresh [[Red chillies|red chillies]], deseeded and sliced\n| 1 [[Iceberg lettuce]], sliced\n}}\n'''dressing'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 220 ml (1/2 cup) [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Nam pla|nam pla]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Jaggery|jaggery]] or [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n}}\n'''garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 8 [[Mint leaves]], chopped\n| 1 [[Red chilli|red chilli]], deseeded and chopped into slices\n| Small bunch of [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], chopped\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Mix the [[Marinade|marinade]] ingredients in a [[Lock and Lock|lock and lock]] box, shake well and [[Marinate|marinate]] for 2 to 3 hours in a cool place\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to a [[Wok|wok]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces together with the [[Garlic|garlic]] until they are [[Browned|browned]] and properly cooked.\n| Allow to cool.\n| Meanwhile, heat the dressing ingredients in a small pan and mix well until the [[Jaggery|jaggery]] has completely dissolved.\n| allow to cool.\n| Add the [[Salad|salad]] items to a large bowl, together with the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, pour over the dressing and sprinkle with the garnish\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nRoasting and crushing [[cashews]] in a [[pestle and mortar]]: I found it easier to first smash the [[cashews]] in a mortar, by covering them with a cloth and bashing them with the pestle through the cloth.                         "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Spicy chicken with coconut and cardamom an Indian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#marinade #chicken #chickendrumsticks #spicychickenwithcoconutandcardamom #coconutmilk #cardamompods #corianderleaves #pestleandmortar #blackpepper #juice #yogurt \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A spicy coconut dish which uses lots of cardamons, an unusual spice, the scent of which always reminds me of\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 6637\n|PortionCalories = 1659\n|DatePublished=7th June 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 9 minutes\n|PrepTime =  24 minutes\n|CookTime =  45 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Spicy chicken with coconut and cardamom recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not the usual Indian meal</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is great if you want a change from the normal take-away.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry, aka Chef]])</span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nA spicy [[Coconut|coconut]] dish which uses lots of [[cardamoms]], an unusual [[Spice|spice]], the scent of which always reminds me of Ralgex!  However, once cooked it just imparts a warm flavour, nothing like the smell of a Gym!\n\nThis needs to be prepared a day in advance for the [[Marinade|marinade]] to penetrate the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n}}\n'''cooking the [[Chicken|chicken]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1.6 kg (3.5 lb) [[Chicken drumsticks|chicken drumsticks]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]]\n| A grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 400ml can [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| 4 large [[Green chillies|green chillies]] de-seeded and finely chopped into rings\n}}\n'''the [[Marinade|marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 teaspoon [[Turmeric powder|turmeric powder]]\n| 1 [[Scant|scant]] tablespoon [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]] in their shells ([[Brown|brown]] and/or green)\n| 1 tablespoon [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Ginger root|ginger root]], peeled and [[Grated|grated]] (use any [[Juice|juice]] too!)\n| 2 [[Green Indian chillies|green indian chillies]], deseeded and thinly sliced\n| 1 teaspoon freshly [[Ground cumin seeds|ground cumin seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon freshly [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]] seeds\n| 80 ml plain [[Natural yogurt|natural yogurt]]\n| [[Zest]] and [[Juice|juice]] of one [[Lime|lime]]\n}}\n'''to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]]\n| 20 ml [[Yogurt|yogurt]] drizzled over the dish\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chicken marinade.jpg|thumb|300px|right|After 30 seconds of shaking!\nImage:Chicken marinade ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Marinade ingredients, ready to mix.\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Remove the skin from the [[Chicken drumsticks|chicken drumsticks]].\n| Cut 3 or 4 deep slashes, right down to the bone of the [[Drumsticks|drumsticks]] so the [[Marinade|marinade]] can penetrate the flesh.\n| Add the [[Chicken drumsticks|chicken drumsticks]] to a large [[Lock and Lock box]].\n| Using a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]], crush the shells of the [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]] to release the [[Seeds|seeds]].  Discard the shells.\n| Crush the [[Cardamom seeds|cardamom seeds]] in the [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] and add to the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces.\n| Add the remaining [[Marinade|marinade]] ingredients to the [[Lock and Lock box|lock and lock box]], close the lid and shake violently for 30 seconds.  That's the mixing done!\n| Leave in a cool place overnight to [[Marinate|marinate]], shaking now and then.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] or large pan and add a good grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| Remove the [[Chicken|chicken]] and set the [[Marinade|marinade]] to one side.\n| Gently [[Brown|brown]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] all over.\n| Add the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and the reserve [[Marinade|marinade]] and ring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| [[Simmer]] for 35 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and a drizzle of [[Yogurt|yogurt]], accompanied by [[Plain rice|plain rice]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#marinade #chicken #chickendrumsticks #spicychickenwithcoconutandcardamom #coconutmilk #cardamompods #corianderleaves #pestleandmortar #blackpepper #juice #yogurt </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

(for two)\n|Servings = Serves 4 to 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 50 minutes\n|PrepTime = 30 minutes\n|CookTime = 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Spicy Chinese cabbage.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">That wok looks very well used</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">It also looks very authentic</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\nA simple spicy vegetable dish that could be served on it's own or as an accompaniment.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 900g (2lb) [[Chinese leaves]] ([[Brassica rapa]], [[Bok choy]], [[Siew choy]], etc)\n| 3 tablespoons [[dark soy sauce]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[sugar]]\n| 1 teaspoon sea [[salt]]\n| 3 tablespoons Chinese rice wine or [[dry sherry]]\n| 6 teaspoons [[vegetable stock]]\n| 1 fresh [[red chilli]] or to taste\n| 2 [[spring onions]] (scallions)\n| 5 fresh [[Shiitake mushrooms]] or\n| 5 dried [[Chinese mushrooms]]\n| 4 tablespoons vegetable oil\n| 1 tablespoon toasted [[sesame seeds]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| If using [[dried mushrooms]], fill a bowl with boiling water and soak them for 30 minutes\n| Slice the mushrooms thinly\n| Cut the [[cabbage]] into 1.5\" pieces, wash and drain\n| Chop [[spring onions]] into &#189;\" pieces - [[on the diagonal]]\n| Finely slice the chillies, removing the seeds if you don't want it too hot\n| Mix together the dark soy, sugar, [[salt]], [[wine]] and [[stock]]\n| Heat the oil in a wok as you would for frying [[onions]], add [[chillies]] and [[spring onions]] and [[stir-fry]] for 2 minutes\n| Add [[cabbage]] and [[mushrooms]], reduce the heat a little and stir-fry for 5 minutes\n| Add the [[soy sauce]] mixture and simmer uncovered for 10 minutes\n| If the liquid has not reduced, you can pour some of the excess away - as happened when I made this for two people.\n| Place in a serving bowl and sprinkle with the toasted [[sesame seeds]]\n| Serve immediately\n}}\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Cabbage]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Cabbage]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Cabbage]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Cabbage]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Cabbage]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Cabbage]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#spicychinesecabbage #springonions #cabbage #sesameseeds #siewchoy #driedmushrooms #mushrooms #bokchoy #redchilli #darksoysauce #onions </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

longer it is [[Marinated|marinated]].\n\nThe [[Salt|salt]] helps to remove a little of the moisture so firming the flesh.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 [[basa]] fillets\n| Juice and zest of one [[Citrus|citrus]] juice, [[Zest|zest]] and [[Nam pla|nam pla]] over the [[Fish|fish]]\n| Place in a lidded [[Lock and Lock]]-style box, shake well and refrigerate for one to four hours\n| In a pan, gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]], celery and red peppers in the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] until soft, about 10 minutes\n| Stir in the [[sugar]], [[vinegar]], chopped [[chilli]], [[Ginger root|ginger root]] and any juice from the marinade\n| [[Oil]] a small ovenproof dish and layer the [[Fish|fish]] and vegetables in it together with all of the juices\n| [[Bake]] covered for 30 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot on a bed of [[Plain boiled rice|plain boiled rice]] sprinkled with the chopped herbs.\n\n===Variations===\nUse [[basa]], [[ling]], [[Halibut|halibut]] or [[conger eel]] as an alternate fish for this dish\n\nThis recipe was the result of a fridge-clean, any combination of your favourite vegetables would be perfect in this Remove and discard the stalks.\n| [[Salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Use a [[Speed peeler|speed peeler]] to remove strips of peel from the [[Cucumber|cucumber]].  Quarter the cucumber lengthways and chop finely - a [[Food processor|food processor]] is good for this.\n| Spread the sliced [[Cucumber|cucumber]] on a large plate and sprinkle liberally with fine [[Salt|salt]].  Leave them to stand for 15 minutes then rinse and drain well.\n| Remove any excess moisture with a [[Paper towel|paper towel]].\n| In the serving bowl, mix the [[Vinegar|vinegar]] and [[Sugar|sugar]] and whisk well until the sugar is dissolved. Add the [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and [[Zest|zest]] and [[Salt|salt]] to taste.\n| Mix in the [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Shallots|shallots]], mints and [[Cucumbers|cucumbers]] with the dressing and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 20 minutes.\n| Mix well before serving.\n}}\n==See also==\n* [[Sweet and sour recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cucumber #sweetandsourcucumbersaladwithmintandchillies #zest #shallots #cucumbers #mintleaves #greenchillies #juice #whitesugar #papertowel #whitewinevinegar </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Each continent has different foods. In Europe, one of the main foods is [[Bread|bread]]. In contrast, Thai people always eat [[Rice|rice]] as a main dish. In this article, I will tell you how to make this tasty dish, [[Sweet Pork Condiment]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]. \n| 5 tablespoons of [[Palm sugar|palm sugar]].\n| 3 tablespoons of water.\n| Half a cup of [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]. \n| 3 tablespoons of [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]]. \n| 350 grams of [[Shoulder|shoulder]], neck or [[Belly of pork|belly of pork]].\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* First step is mix the [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]] and [[Sugar|sugar]] together in a bowl\n* [[Marinate|marinate]] the [[Pork|pork]] in that mixture in the [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]] for at least 36-48 hours, in order to maintain the quality and the taste of the pork.\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Using the [[Steaming|steaming]] pot to [[Boil|boil]] water and [[Steam|steam]] the [[Pork|pork]] about 20 minutes. After the steaming is finished, let the pork [[Rest for|rest for]] about 10 minutes.\n| Cut and slice the [[Pork|pork]] into pieces.\n| Put the [[Palm sugar|palm sugar]] into the pan then stir it over a low heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] until the colour of the [[Sugar|sugar]] is [[Brown|brown]].\n| Add [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]] and water all together then add the [[Pork|pork]] and mix them.\n| Finally, you must [[Simmer|simmer]] it for about 5-10 minutes then mix the [[Pork|pork]] and the [[Sauce|sauce]] together\n}}\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pork #sweetporkcondiment #rice #simmer #palmsugar #lightsoysauce #fishsauce #refrigerator #fried #steam #bellyofpork </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
