The perfect light summer lunch or starter\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1940\n|PortionCalories = 485\n|DatePublished=16th August 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Thai Melon Soup recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Melon \ud83c\udf48 soup \ud83c\udf72</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.2</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Fresh and clean, with that lovely aroma of basil.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis [[Soup|soup]] is ridiculously refreshing and outrageously delicious. The perfect light summer [[Lunch|lunch]] or [[Starter|starter]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 ripe Galia or Honeydew [[Melon|melon]]\n| 1 [[Cucumber|cucumber]]\n| 1 stalk of [[Lemongrass|lemongrass]]\n| 1 heaped teaspoon of freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Ginger|ginger]]\n| A good pinch of finely chopped fresh [[Chilli|chilli]] (more or less to taste)\n| 200ml [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| A large handful of Thai or regular [[Basil|basil]]\n| A small handful of fresh [[Mint|mint]]\n| 1-2 [[Limes|limes]], [[Juice|juice]] and [[Zest|zest]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Halve your [[Melon|melon]]. [[Scoop]] out the [[Seeds|seeds]]. Spoon the flesh from the skin straight into a [[Blender|blender]] or [[Food processor|food processor]].\n| Peel your [[Cucumber|cucumber]]. Roughly chop. Add to the [[Melon|melon]].\n| Bash your [[Lemongrass|lemongrass]] stalk till it flattens and softens a bit. Peel the outer layer away. Thinly slice starting at the base. Finely chop till you have about 1 heaped tsp.\n| Add the [[Lemongrass|lemongrass]] to the [[Blender|blender]]/[[Food processor|food processor]] along with the [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Chilli|chilli]], [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]], [[Basil|basil]], [[Mint|mint]] and the [[Zest|zest]] and [[Juice|juice]] of 1 [[Lime|lime]].\n| Whizz till smooth. Taste. Add more [[Lemongrass|lemongrass]], [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Chilli|chilli]], [[Herbs|herbs]] or [[Lime juice|lime juice]] as needed. Swirl in a bit more [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]], too, if needed (depends on the [[Melon|melon]]\u0092s sweetness).\n| Once it's so good you can't stop eating it, pop it in the [[Freezer|freezer]] to chill quickly or the [[Fridge|fridge]] if you\u0092re serving it later. Lovely garnished with a swirl of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] drizzled on top and some fresh [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]].\n}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Abel and Cole veg box recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n{{Template:Abel and Cole veg box recipes attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#coconutmilk #lemongrass #melon #ginger #chilli #zest #thaimelonsoup #mint #foodprocessor #basil #blender </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Thai Moringa curry with shrimp",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Thai Moringa curry with shrimp recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#shrimp #curry #moringa #tamarind #palmsugar #boil #shrimps #thaimoringacurrywithshrimp #soup #fish #fishsauce \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Kaeng Som Puk Marum or Thai Moringa curry with shrimp has a spicy and sour shrimp curry taste or soup with moringa popular in central of Thailand. }}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1038\n|PortionCalories = 103\n|DatePublished=26th October 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Traditional kaeng som with drumstick pods\n|Servings = Serves 10\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  35 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Kaeng_som-marum.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">An acquired taste.</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I wasn't comfortable with the slime of okra in the version I tried.  Sorry.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaeng_som Kaeng Som] Puk Marum or Thai Moringa [[Curry|curry]] with [[Shrimp|shrimp]] has a spicy and sour shrimp curry taste or [[Soup|soup]] with moringa  popular in central of Thailand.\n[[Nam phrik kaeng som]] is prepared as a base for the [[Curry|curry]], then water and the other [[Ingredient|ingredient]]s are added ,but the main ingredient is moringa. For the preparation of Thai moringa curry the [[Shrimp|shrimp]] and [[Shallots|shallots]] and all of the ingredients are pound with a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]]. \n\n[[Shrimp]] or [[Fish|fish]] may be used as the basic [[Ingredient|ingredient]]. Thai [[moringa]] [[Curry|curry]] with shrimp is usually served with [[Steamed rice|steamed rice]]. \n\nThe [[Curry|curry]] has sour taste, which comes from ripe [[Tamarind|tamarind]] and uses [[Palm sugar|palm sugar]] for sweeten the curry taste.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 800g [[Moringa]]\t\t\n| 40g [[Shrimp]] or [[Fish|fish]]\t\t\t\n| 1g Nam Phrik Kaeng Som\t\n| \u00bc Ripe [[Tamarind|tamarind]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Palm sugar]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Fish sauce]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Peel the [[moringa]], and clean them then cut into the pieces , of about three inches length\n| Bring water to a rapid [[Boil|boil]], add [[Shrimp|shrimp]] and boil until cooked, then remove the [[Shrimps|shrimps]] and cool down. Keep the [[Stock|stock]] for the [[Soup|soup]] base.\n| In the mortar, take 2-3 whole [[Shrimps|shrimps]], and pounded together with [[Nam Phrik Kaeng Som]] until thoroughly mixed.\n| Bring the [[Nam Phrik Kaeng Som]] that was pounded with [[Shrimp|shrimp]] to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] over a high heat for 5 minutes.\n| Add the [[moringa]] and season with [[Palm sugar|palm sugar]], [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]], and concentrated [[Tamarind|tamarind]] [[Juice|juice]] and bring to the [[Boil|boil]]. Add the [[Rest|rest]] of [[Shrimps|shrimps]] and, when it boils again turn off the heat.\n| Serve.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n* Recipe text by [[User:Nutcha Waropashpimarn]]\n==See also==\n\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaeng_som\n* [http://www.recipesource.com/ethnic/asia/thai/02/rec0250.html Nam Phrik Kaeng Som]\n* [http://www.doctor.or.th/article/detail/1053 www.doctor.or.th/article/detail/1053]\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moringa\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#shrimp #curry #moringa #tamarind #palmsugar #boil #shrimps #thaimoringacurrywithshrimp #soup #fish #fishsauce </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Thanks Panrapee</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Looks like a fabulous way to serve oysters - can't wait to try this at home.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThai [[Fried|fried]] [[Oysters|oysters]] (Thai : &#3627;&#3629;&#3618;&#3607;&#3629;&#3604;(Hoii-thot), [[Chinese]] : &#3629;&#3629;&#3626;&#3656;&#3623;&#3609;(Or-Suan)) is a famous fast food in Thailand that you can find on many street corners in Bangkok and also popular in other places such as Taiwan, Hong Kong, and the Philippines. The main ingredients are [[Flour|flour]], [[Spice|spice]], [[Egg|egg]], and [[Oyster|oyster]] serve with [[Bean sprouts|bean sprouts]] and [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]] on the hot plate. This food is very popular because there are five categories of nutrients.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 10 small [[Oysters|oysters]] (or [[Mussels|mussels]], [[Squid|squid]], or [[Seafood|seafood]] as you prefer)\n| 2 tablespoons [[Rice flour|rice flour]]\n| &#189; tablespoon [[Cassava|cassava]] [[Starch|starch]] \n| 1 cup fresh [[Bean sprouts|bean sprouts]]\n| 3 tablespoons cold water\n| &#188; teaspoon Thai [[Pepper powder|pepper powder]]\n| &#188; teaspoon chopped [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| &#188; teaspoon chopped [[Onion|onion]]\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]]\n| 1 [[free range egg]]\n| [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] for cooking\n}}\n'''[[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]] for [[Oysters|oysters]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 tablespoons sweet [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Wash [[Oysters|oysters]] in cold water, then [[Poached|poached]] and drain well.\n| Mix [[Cassava|cassava]] [[Starch|starch]] and [[Rice flour|rice flour]] with the water and mix well.\n| Heat the [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] in a pan. When the [[Oil|oil]] is hot, pour the mixed [[Flour|flour]] and [[Oysters|oysters]] together.\n| Add the [[Egg|egg]] after [[Batter|batter]] is set. Make a hole in the centre with a spatula, cook until golden crispy.\n| Pour a little more [[Oil|oil]] in the pan, [[Fry|fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Bean sprouts|bean sprouts]] until it heated.\n| Mix all ingredients, then season with [[Fish sauce|fish sauce]], [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Onion|onion]] and Thai [[Pepper powder|pepper powder]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe it with a [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]].\n==See also==\n\n* http://pantip.com/topic/30652509, &#3627;&#3629;&#3618;&#3607;&#3629;&#3604;&#3649;&#3611;&#3657;&#3591;&#3585;&#3619;&#3629;&#3610; &#3626;&#3641;&#3605;&#3619;&#3629;&#3619;&#3656;&#3629;&#3618;&#3648;&#3627;&#3634;&#3632; (&#3610;&#3656;&#3591;&#3610;&#3658;&#3591;, June 26, 2014)\n* http://www.pim.in.th/one-dish-food/56-sea-[[Mussel|mussel]]-[[Fried|fried]].html, &#3627;&#3629;&#3618;&#3607;&#3629;&#3604; (&#3614;&#3636;&#3617; @ &#3588;&#3619;&#3633;&#3623;&#3610;&#3657;&#3634;&#3609;&#3614;&#3636;&#3617;, July 17, 2009)\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#oysters #chillisauce #beansprouts #pepperpowder #onion #riceflour #cassava #fishsauce #vegetableoil #fried #starch </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This is the recipe. \n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4498\n|PortionCalories = 1124\n|DatePublished=24th October 2014\n|Author=Panrapee Satienpisarn\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 1 day, 1 hour\n|PrepTime = 1 day\n|CookTime =  1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:Wewe recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Authentic!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Sure is sweet and sticky!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Thai sweet sticky rice]] - Thai [[Steamed]] Sticky [[Rice]] with [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] (Khao Nieaw Moon) has been a popular Thai [[Dessert|dessert]] for many centuries. Sweet sticky rice is different from Sticky rice which is non-flavored. It has a few easy steps. When finished, you can just eat sweet sticky rice, but many Thai [[Fruits|fruits]] and [[Desserts|desserts]] can be eaten with sweet sticky rice such as, eat with [[Mangoes|mangoes]], [[Egg custard|egg custard]] (Sang Kha Ya), and durian. All of these are very popular for foreigners.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| &#189; kg. Kieaw Ngu sticky [[Rice|rice]] (soak in water 1 night) \n| 3 Tsp. [[salt]]\n| 400 grams [[sugar]]\n| 500 grams [[Coconut milk]]\n| 3 [[Pandanus]] leaf\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Soak the [[Rice|rice]] in water overnight\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Soak the [[Rice|rice]] in one cup water for 20-30 minutes. Then rinse with clean water 1 time.\n| Place a white cloth in a [[Steaming|steaming]] pot. And [[Steam|steam]] sticky [[Rice|rice]] for 40 minutes until cooked.\n| After 30 minutes has passed, add [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]], [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Salt|salt]], and [[Pandanus|pandanus]] leaves into the pot. Then [[Boil|boil]] for 10 minutes.\n| When 40 minutes has passed, add sticky [[Rice|rice]] into the pot. Follow with [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] and stir to combine. [[Steam]] for 10 minutes.\n| Stir sticky [[Rice|rice]] again. Mix thoroughly and [[Steam|steam]] more for 10 minutes.\n| Top with [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] before serving. Ready to eat.\n}}\n==See also==\n\n* Kasma Loha-unchit (1995), [[Pandanus]] Leaf \u0096Bai Dteuy http://www.thaifoodandtravel.com/ingredients/pandan.html \n* Chef Lek (2012), &#3586;&#3657;&#3634;&#3623;&#3648;&#3627;&#3609;&#3637;&#3618;&#3623;&#3617;&#3641;&#3609; , http://www.foodtravel.tv/recfoodShow_Detail.aspx?viewId=496\n* Darlene Schmidt, Classic Thai [[Mango]] Sticky [[Rice pudding|rice pudding]] (Khao Niaow Ma Muang) http://thaifood.about.com/od/thaidesserts/r/mangoricepuddin.htm\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #coconutmilk #steam #thaisweetstickyrice #pandanus #steamed #mango #ricepudding #steaming #dessert #thairecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Hers was an adapted version of [http://www.bbq-nl.com/2009/07/the-renowned-mr-brown.html the original] (''Dutch'').  I have further adapted [http://www.flickr.com/photos/fotoosvanrobin/6308694585/ hers].\n\nThe [[Meat|meat]] is great as a main meal with [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[potatoes]] or with a salad or even as a [[Sandwich|sandwich]] filler.  My favourite way is to have it as a [[Kebab|kebab]]-type filling in [[Pitta bread|pitta bread]] with [[Salad|salad]].\n\nI have included this in the North American recipe category as a homage to the original.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.3 kg (3 lb) boneless [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]].\n| 1 tablespoon coarsely [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Smoked paprika powder|smoked paprika powder]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 4 tablespoons cane [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Coarse sea salt|coarse sea salt]]\n| 2 teaspoons kona karashi (Japanese [[Mustard powder|mustard powder]])\n| 2 tablespoons [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Ginger powder|ginger powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cayenne pepper|cayenne pepper]] or a [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] mix of your choice\n| &#189; cup  [[Shaoxing rice wine]], [[Sherry|sherry]] or even spirit of your choice\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and roughly chopped (or equivalent in [[Spring onions|spring onions]] or [[Leeks|leeks]])\n| 1 [[Apple|apple]], peeled, cored and cubed\n\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - Oriental slow roast.jpg|After 4 hours...\nImage:The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - Oriental slow roast marinaded.jpg|Ready to cook\n</gallery>\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3), [fan oven 140\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the [[Spices|spices]], cut deep slashes all over the meat and rub the mixture well into the pork.\n| Place in a [[Lock & Lock]]-style box and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 24 hours, shaking up now and again.\n| Chop the [[Apple|apple]] and [[Onion|onion]] and place in the base of a [[Baking|baking]] dish\n| Sit the [[Pork|pork]] on top, pour over the [[Wine|wine]] and add a little more rub to the top\n| Cover with [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]] and cook for 4 hours\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nShred with two forks and serve in [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] with a [[Green salad|green salad]].\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you are not to use it all in one go, only shred what you will use straight away, store the remainder in the [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]], unshredded in a [[Lock & Lock box]]. This way it will stay moist. \nFollow the [[RSPCA Think Pig Checklist]] to make sure that your [[Pork|pork]] has come from pigs that have been reared to higher welfare standards.\n{{Template:See-also-pulled-pork}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:FotoosVanRobin recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#therenownedmrbrownpulledporkoriental #apple #onion #pulledpork #pork #sandwich #pittabreads #wine #coarseseasalt #miseenplace #smokedpaprikapowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Yellow curry; a  recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#babysweetcorn #coconutmilk #potatoes #chicken #fried #currypaste #onions #nampla #yellowcurry #boil #curry \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Yellow curry (thai: \u0e41\u0e01\u0e07\u0e01\u0e30\u0e2b\u0e23\u0e35\u0e48, RTGS: kaeng kari, k\u025b\u02d0\u014b kar\u00ec\u02d0; chinese  often found in Western Thai restaurants.\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 6256\n|PortionCalories = 1564\n|DatePublished=29th December 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 35 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes \n|CookTime = 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Kaeng kari kai_jp.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I love Chinese curries</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not the same as an Indian curry, but none the less, very good. I agree, Cock Brand curry pastes are very good.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nYellow [[Curry|curry]] ([[Thai]]: &#3649;&#3585;&#3591;&#3585;&#3632;&#3627;&#3619;&#3637;&#3656;, RTGS: [[Kaeng kari|kaeng kari]],  [k&#603;&#720;&#331; kar\u00ec&#720;]; [[Chinese]]: &#40643;&#21654;&#21937;) is one of the more popular [[Curries|curries]] often found in Western Thai restaurants.\n\nMy favourite curry pastes are the [[Cock Brand pastes]].  They go off quickly, even if [[Refrigerated|refrigerated]], but if they are [[Frozen|frozen]], they keep for years.  Even better, you can just remove a few tablespoons of the curry paste even it is frozen.  Brilliant!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 3 tablespoons of yellow [[Curry paste|curry paste]]\n| 400g can of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]]\n| 450g (1 lb) of [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces.  Breast [[Meat|meat]] is good but I feel the cuts with [[bones]] impart more flavour\n| 3 medium [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and cut into quarters\n| 125g packet of fresh [[Baby sweet corn|baby sweetcorn]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Nam pla|nam pla]] ([[Fish sauce|fish sauce]])\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 30g [[Fried]] [[Onions|onions]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Part [[Boil|boil]] the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] for 7 minutes and set to one side\n| Cut your [[Chicken|chicken]] into bite-sized pieces, cutting through the bone with a cleaver if needed\n| Halve the [[Baby sweetcorn|baby sweetcorn]] cobs\n| Mix the can of [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] well and add to a pan or [[Wok|wok]] together with the yellow [[Curry paste|curry paste]]\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, [[Potatoes|potatoes]], [[Baby sweetcorn|baby sweetcorn]] cobs and [[Nam pla|nam pla]]\n| Bring the [[Coconut milk|coconut milk]] to the [[Boil|boil]] and reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe garnished with crispy [[Fried|fried]] [[Onions|onions]] on a bed of [[Plain rice|plain rice]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Thai recipes]]\n[[Category:Vietnamese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#babysweetcorn #coconutmilk #potatoes #chicken #fried #currypaste #onions #nampla #yellowcurry #boil #curry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
